<username>Laura Ricci<//username><time>1618508178643</time>< Rate>

< text>
Long Covid and infection burst a tooth. During the pandemic, many dentists were closed, but SmileSF was taking patients and had good reviews. The diagnosis was to address a variety of issues to give me the best chance of success with a crown on the broken tooth: Gum treatment was needed to clear infection, home care would be required to heal the gums. Next, the broken tooth was flanked by two teeth with old fillings, so those fillings were ready to be replaced, and the best time to do it would be during the clean out and installation of the new crown. I could understand it would be dicey dealing with either of those fillings later. So over the last 6 weeks I've had all this work done. The bonus is that my Long Covid episodes (which had escalated during the few weeks before my tooth burst) have subsided a great deal. Causation or correlation? Who knows? Long Covid is a mystery at this point. But many of us who had Covid-19 are having a variety of dental problems. SmileSF is practicing good protocols to keep them and we safe from re-infection. If you are cohort 2 (as I am) and episodes are increasing, checking for infection of your gums and teeth might be worthwhile. This office is struggling a bit with the Pandemic protocols, as everyone is. But they are fully equipped and careful. I would recommend Dr. Farah Sefidvash.< /text>

<time>1602486086666</time>< text>
Newly opened areas for foot tragic flow; gives this place a welcomed new  feel!  Sunday's only 9am 5pm

No parking. Parking lot was full. If you can find one, street parking available.

Admission...$5

The line to get in was long. However, the line moved quickly and we were in!

100 +  friendly vendors offering you the best deal they can.

Live DJ Killing it!
And Various Music playing here and there as you stroll looking for those sleepers (hidden treasure)!

Shady areas to relax/ post.

Delicious Food trucks to fuel you when you get the munchies. And yes, Rest rooms available and clean.

If you enjoy:
A lively atmosphere.
Youthful spirited energy.
Friendly faces. And a barrage of clothing, vintage items, oddities, Art,  etc.

Then I'll see you there!</text>

< Text>
The place to find unique one-off items. From clothing and accessories to furniture and trinkets. I love wandering around the aisles, getting lost and promising myself not to spend any more money. Hard to do.

They raised entrance fee prices from $3 to $5. Cash is best to have on you for most of these merchants.

Come right when it opens to find the best items. Or if you just want to browse, take your time and get here before they close or else you‚Äôll get a million reminders on the loud speaker about closing in x-amount of minutes.

There‚Äôs a cute food court area - all located out doors. Get coffees here, rest your legs and unwind.

< review>
I didn't know this place before until my daughter who is Miss Jr Teen Hollywood was there to sell some cookies in order to help some non proffit organizations. This place remind me of my home town Tlacolula plaza because there are a lot of different vendors so you can enjoy different kind of foods and flavors. < review>
I could go on and on about this flea market - I have devotedly attended this Sunday tradition for years now and have watched it steadily grow in size, vendors, and popularity.  You can find an eclectic variety of wares here: vintage clothing, artisan and vintage jewelry, houseplants, antiques, local artists, new furniture from local craftsmen, food for all tastes and diets, knick-knacks galore, and even more items in between. Most vendors inside accept cash and cards, but be prepared for the cash-only entrance fee of $5. You‚Äôre guaranteed to find something you didn‚Äôt know you wanted every time you go.< /review>

It carries a $5 entry, but once you're in you're greeted with mostly vintage clothes, a few succulents and/or house plants vendors, some vintage print places, local Jewelers, vintage furniture, and a pretty great coffee place. It's more of a quirky outdoor home decor shop with a cover fee, but it does have its gems. Go here for clothing, or home decor. Don't come here for bargain hunting and lots of treasure hunting.</Review>< Pics>

As my friend says, it's like an outdoor goodwill, so you don't get the musty smells.  Are you spending an arm and leg on stuff you can get for a few dollars at Goodwill?  Probably!  But the goods are always unique and there are also almost always celebrities if that's your thing.

There is always awesome music in the food area.  And the food isn't bad either!  The guy in the corner doing corn bowls is awesome with delicious kombucha on tap.  Other notable eateries include the crepe place and there are always samples of fries.<//Review><Pictures>None</Pictures><Response>None< /Response><GmapID>0x80c2beccfa5466f5:0x5f3fd735a7af1c9e<//GmapID></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Its a street market showcasing local artistry and people's vintage finds. What other would call junk could also be another person's treasure. No shortage of old clothes and ornaments. There's a vendor there that has a whole department store section for aloha shirts for 7.00. Great fit for summer or for a gift for your trendy teen. It's bigger than you think so take the time to explore. Also, say hi to all the dogs you'll see. Came around 1:20, didn't find parking until 2:00 so I suggest coming early. There's also a mini street market across the street. It's a great Instagram photo spot due to the fact that there's an angel wing mural at the entrance of it. Great place to visit for 2 or so hours.< /review>

< Review>
Of the flea market offerings in LA, this is a big one.  However, the dominant item is clothes, clothes, clothes.  If you are looking for curated/vintage home goods or local artists, artisans, etc, this swap meet does have some, but they are few in number compared to the clothing offerings.  It's mainly a younger crowd, so whatever used-clothing trend is happening at the moment for that audience, you'll find a lot of here.<//Review>

The hot spot for LA‚Äôs urban dwellers every Sunday, Fairfax High School parking lot is filled to the max of hipsters and kiosks ready to upscale your wardrobe or you interior decorating. Entry fee is under $5 and you can literally spend a whole day here checking out the shops, some live music and a delicious snow cone. Every trip to the Flea Market I walk away with new hand crafted jewelry or a groovy pair of sunglasses. Do yourself a favor and brave the parking to come wander around the asphalt, it will not disappoint.</text>
